     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Texas_at_Austin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Texas_at_Austin_alumni" title="List of University of Texas at Austin alumni">List of University of Texas at Austin alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Dell,_square_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg/170px-Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg/255px-Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg/340px-Michael_Dell%2C_square_crop.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Dell,_square_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dell" title="Michael Dell">Michael Dell</a> started 
        <i>PC's Limited</i> (the precursor to 
        <a href="/wiki/Dell_Computers" title="Dell Computers" class="mw-redirect">Dell Computers</a>) before 
        <a href="/wiki/Dropping_out" title="Dropping out">dropping out</a> of the University of Texas.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Texas_Exes" title="Texas Exes">Texas Exes</a> is the official UT alumni organization.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_Alcalde" title="The Alcalde">The Alcalde</a>, founded in 1913 and pronounced ?all-call-day,? is the university's alumni magazine.</p> 
     <p>Over 15 graduates have served in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Bentsen" title="Lloyd Bentsen">Lloyd Bentsen</a> '42, who served as both a U.S. Senator and U.S. Representative, as well as being the 1988 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> Vice Presidential nominee.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Presidential cabinet members include former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Baker" title="James Baker">James Baker</a> '57,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> former United States Secretary of Education <a href="/wiki/William_J._Bennett" title="William J. Bennett" class="mw-redirect">William J. Bennett</a>, and former United States Secretary of Commerce <a href="/wiki/Donald_Evans" title="Donald Evans">Donald Evans</a> '73. Former <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a> '73 and daughter <a href="/wiki/Jenna_Bush" title="Jenna Bush" class="mw-redirect">Jenna</a> '04 both graduated from Texas,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as former <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Bird_Johnson" title="Lady Bird Johnson">Lady Bird Johnson</a> '33 &amp; '34 and her eldest daughter <a href="/wiki/Lynda_Bird_Johnson_Robb" title="Lynda Bird Johnson Robb">Lynda</a>. In foreign governments, the university has been represented by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Bela%C3%BAnde_Terry" title="Fernando Bela&uacute;nde Terry">Fernando Bela&uacute;nde Terry</a> '36 (42nd President of <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mostafa_Chamran" title="Mostafa Chamran">Mostafa Chamran</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Defense" title="Minister of Defense" class="mw-redirect">Minister of Defense</a> for <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_al-Tariki" title="Abdullah al-Tariki" class="mw-redirect">Abdullah al-Tariki</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>). Additionally, the Prime Minister of the Palestinian National Authority, <a href="/wiki/Salam_Fayyad" title="Salam Fayyad">Salam Fayyad</a>, graduated from the university with a PhD in economics.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mrsbush-20060206.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Mrsbush-20060206.jpg/170px-Mrsbush-20060206.jpg" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Mrsbush-20060206.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Mrsbush-20060206.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mrsbush-20060206.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Former 
        <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a> '73 received an M.L.S. from the University of Texas.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Alumni in academia include the 26th President of <a href="/wiki/The_College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="The College of William &amp; Mary" class="mw-redirect">The College of William &amp; Mary</a> <a href="/wiki/Gene_Nichol" title="Gene Nichol">Gene Nichol</a> '76, the 10th President of <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Brown" title="Robert A. Brown">Robert A. Brown</a> '73 &amp; '75,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 8th President of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a> <a href="/wiki/John_R._Hubbard" title="John R. Hubbard">John R. Hubbard</a>. The University also graduated <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">Alan Bean</a> '55, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_walked_on_the_Moon" title="List of people who have walked on the Moon" class="mw-redirect">fourth man to walk on the Moon</a>. Additionally, alumni who have served as business leaders include <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_Corporation" title="ExxonMobil Corporation" class="mw-redirect">ExxonMobil Corporation</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a> '75, <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a> founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dell" title="Michael Dell">Michael Dell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gary_C._Kelly" title="Gary C. Kelly">Gary C. Kelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>'s CEO.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_clemens_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Roger_clemens_2004.jpg/170px-Roger_clemens_2004.jpg" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Roger_clemens_2004.jpg/255px-Roger_clemens_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Roger_clemens_2004.jpg/340px-Roger_clemens_2004.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_clemens_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Alumnus 
        <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clemens" title="Roger Clemens">Roger Clemens</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/MLB" title="MLB" class="mw-redirect">MLB</a> pitcher and seven-time 
        <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> winner
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In literature and journalism, the school has produced <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Gail_Caldwell" title="Gail Caldwell">Gail Caldwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Sargent" title="Ben Sargent">Ben Sargent</a> '70. <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite" title="Walter Cronkite">Walter Cronkite</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/CBS_Evening_News" title="CBS Evening News">CBS Evening News</a> anchor once called the most trusted man in America, attended the University of Texas at Austin, as did <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> anchor <a href="/wiki/Betty_Nguyen" title="Betty Nguyen">Betty Nguyen</a> '95. Alumnus <a href="/wiki/J._M._Coetzee" title="J. M. Coetzee">J. M. Coetzee</a> also received the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>. Novelist <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Benson" title="Raymond Benson">Raymond Benson</a> ('78) was the official author of James Bond novels between 1996?2002, the only American to be commissioned to pen them. <a href="/wiki/Donna_Alvermann" title="Donna Alvermann">Donna Alvermann</a>, a distinguished research professor at the University of Georgia, Department of Education also graduated from the University of Texas, as did <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Clift" title="Wallace Clift">Wallace Clift</a> ('49) and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Dalby_Clift" title="Jean Dalby Clift">Jean Dalby Clift</a> ('50, J.D. '52), authors of several books in the fields of psychology of religion and spiritual growth. <a href="/wiki/Alireza_Jafarzadeh" title="Alireza Jafarzadeh">Alireza Jafarzadeh</a> the author of &quot;The Iran Threat: President Ahmadinejad and the Coming Nuclear Crisis&quot; and television commentator ('82, MS)</p> 
     <p>Several musicians and entertainers attended the University, though most dropped out to pursue their respective careers. <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, the American singer who was posthumously inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> and who received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a> attended the university,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> as did February 1955 <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Playboy_Playmate" title="Playboy Playmate">Playmate of the Month</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" title="Golden Globe" class="mw-redirect">Golden Globe</a> recipient <a href="/wiki/Jayne_Mansfield" title="Jayne Mansfield">Jayne Mansfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Composer <a href="/wiki/Harold_Morris_(composer)" title="Harold Morris (composer)">Harold Morris</a> is a 1910 graduate. Noted film director, cinematographer, writer, and editor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rodriguez" title="Robert Rodriguez">Robert Rodriguez</a> is a Longhorn, as are actors <a href="/wiki/Eli_Wallach" title="Eli Wallach">Eli Wallach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_McConaughey" title="Matthew McConaughey">Matthew McConaughey</a>. Rodriguez dropped out of the university after two years to pursue his career in Hollywood, but he officially completed his degree from the Radio-Television-Film department on May 23, 2009. Rodriguez also gave the keynote address at the university-wide commencement ceremony. Radio-Television-Film alumni <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dennis_(director)" title="Mark Dennis (director)">Mark Dennis</a> and Ben Foster took their award winning feature film, <a href="/wiki/Strings_(2012_film)" title="Strings (2012 film)" class="mw-redirect">Strings</a>, to the American film festival circuit in 2011. Web and television actress <a href="/wiki/Felicia_Day" title="Felicia Day">Felicia Day</a> and film actress <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Zellweger" title="Ren&eacute;e Zellweger">Ren&eacute;e Zellweger</a> also attended the university. Day graduated with dual degrees in music performance (violin) and mathematics, while Zellweger graduated with a BA in English. Writer, recording artist <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Sandifer" title="Phillip Sandifer">Phillip Sandifer</a> attended the university and graduated with a degree in History. <a href="/wiki/Farrah_Fawcett" title="Farrah Fawcett">Farrah Fawcett</a>, one of the original <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie%27s_Angels" title="Charlie's Angels">Charlie's Angels</a></i>, left after her junior year to pursue a modeling career. Actor <a href="/wiki/Owen_Wilson" title="Owen Wilson">Owen Wilson</a> and writer/director <a href="/wiki/Wes_Anderson" title="Wes Anderson">Wes Anderson</a> each attended the university. There they wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Bottle_Rocket" title="Bottle Rocket">Bottle Rocket</a></i> together which became Anderson's first feature film. Another notable writer, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Thomas_(writer)" title="Rob Thomas (writer)">Rob Thomas</a> graduated with a BA in History in 1987 and went on to write the young adult novel <i><a href="/wiki/Rats_Saw_God" title="Rats Saw God">Rats Saw God</a></i> and created the series <i><a href="/wiki/Veronica_Mars" title="Veronica Mars">Veronica Mars</a></i>. Notable illustrator, writer and alum, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.harpercollins.com/authors/11820/Felicia_Bond/index.aspx">Felicia Bond</a>, is best known for her illustrations in the <i>If You Give...</i> children's books series, starting with <i><a href="/wiki/If_You_Give_a_Mouse_a_Cookie" title="If You Give a Mouse a Cookie">If You Give a Mouse a Cookie</a></i>. Chinese singer-songwriter, producer, actress <a href="/wiki/Cindy_Yen" title="Cindy Yen">Cindy Yen</a> (birth name Cindy Wu) graduated with double degrees in Music (piano performance) and Broadcast Journalism in 2008.</p> 
     <p>Many alumni have found success in professional sports. Legendary pro football coach <a href="/wiki/Tom_Landry" title="Tom Landry">Tom Landry</a> '49 attended the university as an industrial engineering major but interrupted his education after a semester to serve in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Corps" title="United States Army Air Corps">United States Army Air Corps</a> during World War II. Following the war, he returned to the university and played fullback and defensive back on the Longhorns' bowl-game winners on New Year's Day of 1948 and 1949. Seven-time <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a>-winner <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clemens" title="Roger Clemens">Roger Clemens</a> entered the <a href="/wiki/MLB" title="MLB" class="mw-redirect">MLB</a> after helping the Longhorns win the <a href="/wiki/1983_College_World_Series" title="1983 College World Series">1983 College World Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Three-time <a href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA" class="mw-redirect">NBA</a> scoring champion <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Durant" title="Kevin Durant">Kevin Durant</a> entered the <a href="/wiki/2007_NBA_Draft" title="2007 NBA Draft" class="mw-redirect">2007 NBA Draft</a> and was selected second overall behind <a href="/wiki/Greg_Oden" title="Greg Oden">Greg Oden</a>, after sweeping National Player of the Year honors, becoming the first freshman to win any of the awards. After becoming became the first freshman in school history to lead Texas in scoring and being named the Big 12 Freshman of the Year, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Gibson" title="Daniel Gibson">Daniel Gibson</a> entered the <a href="/wiki/2006_NBA_Draft" title="2006 NBA Draft" class="mw-redirect">2006 NBA Draft</a> and was selected in the second round by the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers" title="Cleveland Cavaliers">Cleveland Cavaliers</a>. Several Olympic medalists have also attended the school, including <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> athletes <a href="/wiki/Ian_Crocker" title="Ian Crocker">Ian Crocker</a> '05 (swimming world record holder and two-time Olympic gold medalist) and 4x400m relay defending Olympic gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Sanya_Richards" title="Sanya Richards" class="mw-redirect">Sanya Richards</a> '06.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Retton" title="Mary Lou Retton">Mary Lou Retton</a> (the first female gymnast outside Eastern Europe to win the Olympic all-around title, five-time Olympic medalist, and 1984 <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> Sportswoman of the Year) also attended the university.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Also an alumnus is Dr. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cade" title="Robert Cade">Robert Cade</a>, the inventor of the sport drink <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a>.</p> 
     <p>Other notable alumni include prominent businessman <a href="/wiki/Red_McCombs" title="Red McCombs">Red McCombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diane_Pamela_Wood" title="Diane Pamela Wood" class="mw-redirect">Diane Pamela Wood</a>, a judge on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Seventh_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit</a>, and astrophysicist <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a>. Also an alumnus is Admiral <a href="/wiki/William_H._McRaven" title="William H. McRaven">William H. McRaven</a>, credited for organizing and executing <a href="/wiki/Operation_Neptune%27s_Spear" title="Operation Neptune's Spear" class="mw-redirect">Operation Neptune's Spear</a>, the special ops raid that led to the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden" title="Death of Osama bin Laden">death of Osama bin Laden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

       <li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._colleges_and_universities_by_endowment">&quot;List of U.S. colleges and universities by endowment&quot;</a>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Texas+at+Austin&amp;rft.btitle=List+of+U.S.+colleges+and+universities+by+endowment&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FList_of_U.S._colleges_and_universities_by_endowment&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As required by the Texas Constitution <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.capitol.state.tx.us/txconst/sections/cn000700-001800.html">[2]</a>, the University of Texas System gets two-thirds of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Available_University_Fund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Available University Fund (page does not exist)">Available University Fund</a>, the annual distribution of PUF income. A regental policy <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.utsystem.edu/OGC/RegentalPolicies/AUFspend.htm">[3]</a> requires that <i>at least</i> 45 percent of this money go to the university for &quot;program enrichment.&quot; By taking two-thirds and multiplying it by 45 percent, we get 30 percent which is the <i>minimum</i> amount of AUF income that can be distributed to the school under current policies. The Regents, however, can and do decide to allocate additional amounts to the university. Also, the majority of the University of Texas system share of the AUF is used for its debt service <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>, some of which were issued for the benefit of the Austin campus <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.utsystem.edu/CONT/REPORTS/LARs/AUFLAR-102704.pdf">[4]</a>. One should note that the Regents are free to change the 45 percent minimum of the University of Texas System share going to the Austin campus at any time, although doing so might be difficult politically.</span></li>
